Jamison Brereton

63
Indra
Nodhas Gautama
9 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The fondness of Nodhas for initial repetition is on display in this hymn, where almost every verse begins with t(u)v├бm тАЬyou,тАЭ with a distracted vocative ind(a)ra positioned after an early caesura. The hymn lacks the verbal intricacy of the last two (I.61тАУ62), though it is full of philological problems.
The tone of the hymn also differs from the two previous ones: it is far more martial and concerned with IndraтАЩs fearsome power. His aggressive power, even just after birth, is highlighted in verse 1, and the following verses quickly allude to the destruction of various foes, usually for the benefit of one of his clients (e.g., Kutsa, vs. 3) or for mortals in general. Like the last two hymns, this one ends with a sum
mary verse applicable to the тАЬFallow-bay-yokingтАЭ oblation.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, you are the mighty one, who, becoming manifest in (the hour of) alarm, did sustain by your energies heaven and earth; then, through fear of you, all creatures, and the mountains, and all other vast and solid things, trembled, like the (tremulous) rays of the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By your energies: balaiс╕е = by strength;

┼Ъuс╣гmaiс╕е = the driers up (of enemies)

Jamison Brereton

You are great, Indra, you who, on just being born, with your tempests put heaven and earth in (the path of your) onslaught,
so that all the vast masses, even the mountains, though firmly fixed, stirred like dust-motes in fear of you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The very first hemistich of this hymn presents us with a syntactic problem: although the most natural way to read this is with a rel. clause beginning with y├│ ha and continuing through the second p─Бda, the verb there, dh─Бс╕е, is unaccented. There are three possible ways to handle this. The first, the one I followed in the published translation, is to assume that dh─Бс╕е got de-accented for some reason. Several possible reasons are available, though none of them strong: 1) it lost its accent redactionally from being matched to (properly) unaccented dh─Бt in 2b, also at the end of its hemistich; 2) the same idiom ├бme (тАж) dh─Бt is found in nearby I.67.3 (unfortunately by a different poet) and this caused the loss of accent redactionally; 3) because the 2nd hemistich of the verse in question is also a subordinate clause (beginning y├бd dha), the previous subordinate clause lost its verbal accent and became a kind of тАЬhonoraryтАЭ main clause, because the action of cd is based on that of the relative clause that precedes it.

(This seems to be one possibility that Oldenberg floats, though he is rather sketchy about it.) Though Geldner does not mention the lack of accent, he tr. the whole as a rel clause.

The other two ways to deal with the problem involve having the rel. clause end at the end of the first p─Бda. Oldenberg also suggested the possibility that the rel. cl. is limited to y├│ ha ┼Ы├║с╣гmaiс╕е. Renou, Hoffmann (1967: 181), and Witzel Got┼Н all follow this path, with tr. of the type тАЬYou are great, Indra, who are (so) because of your ┼Ы├║с╣гma.тАЭ I rejected that because of its awkwardness, although I recognized that it solves the accentless verb problem, since the main clause can occupy p─Бda b without problem.

A third way, also ending the relative clause with the end of the first p─Бda, seems to me to be less clumsy, and that is to make all of the first p─Бda the relative clause.

Though y├бс╕е appears to be fairly far into that clause, in fact it is not preceded by more than one constituent (plus a vocative, which doesnтАЩt count). This produces a tr.

тАЬ(you) who are great because of your ┼Ы├║с╣гma-, you placed тАж.тАЭ This actually has a parallel in IV.22.3 y├│ dev├бс╕е тАж, mah├│ v─Б╠Бjebhir mah├бdbhi┼Ы ca ┼Ы├║с╣гmaiс╕е тАЬThe god who тАж is great by reason of his prizes and his great ┼Ы├║с╣гma.тАЭ I would therefore now change the tr. accordingly, to this third option.

The next problem in this half verse is the construction of ├бme тИЪdh─Б. All the standard tr. render it more or less as тАЬyou put Heaven and Earth in panic/fear.тАЭ This makes sense of the syntax, but attenuates the meaning of the noun: ├бma- is an attack or onslaught, or more abstractly offensive power, whereas тАШpanic, fearтАЩ suggests the opposite. Therefore, although slightly more machinery is required, I tr. this idiom (found also in I.67.3, IV.17.7) as тАЬput X in the path/way of your onslaught.тАЭ Notice that here Nodhas manages to deploy a perfectly orthodox de-coupled dual dvandva for Heaven and Earth (dy─Б╠Бv─Б тАж pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б). See remarks on I.61.14, 62.8.

The subject NP(s) of cd are neatly interwoven: with v├н┼Ыv─Б тАж ├бbhv─Б (neut.) chained with gir├бya┼Ы cid тАж dс╣Ыс╕╖с╕е─Б╠Бsaс╕е (masc.).

Hoffmann (p. 181) argues convincingly that na├нjan should not be interpreted as n├б a├нjan with the Pp., but with the injunctive ├йjan.

Griffith

THOU art the Mighty One; when born, O Indra, with power thou terrifiedst earth and heaven;
When, in their fear of thee, all firm-set mountains and monstrous creatures shook like dust before thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Indra, you harness your variously moving horses, your praiser plural ces your thunderbolt in your hands, wherewith, accom;oisher of undesired acts, you assail your enemies, and glorified by many, destroy their numerous cities.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aviharyatakratu = aprepsita karman, he does actions undesired by his foes

Jamison Brereton

When, Indra, you pursued hither your two fallow bays who follow separate commandments, the singer placed the mace in your two arms, with which, o you whose resolve is not to be deflected, you dispatch the foes and their many strongholds, o much invoked one.184 I.64

Jamison Brereton Notes

If my new parsing of the syntax of vs. 1 is correct, these two verses are structurally parallel, with a relative/subordinate clause in a, the main clause in b, and a further subordinate clause, esp. dependent on the main clause, in cd.

Note the phonological trick, where (─Б╠Б) y├бd dh├б(r─л) opens 2a, apparently matching y├бd dha of 1c (which in turn shows dha for ha, found in the grammatically different rel. clause y├│ ha in 1a). The verse ends with more alliteration: d p├║ra(с╕е)…

puru- … p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е.

The meaning of v├нvrata-, several times of IndraтАЩs horses, but also with a few other referents, isnтАЩt entirely clear, because it depends on which of the many value of v├н to assume. I favor тАШhaving separate commandmentsтАЩ, that is, acting independently but each in obedience to Indra, but it could also mean тАШwithout commandmentsтАЩ (which must underlie GeldnerтАЩs тАШwiderspenstigeтАЩ [stubborn], followed by Hoffmann [but with ?]).

The c p─Бda lacks a caesura and in its place has a somewhat bizarre compound, voc. aviharyata-kratu-. The second member is clear, and the whole must be a bahuvr─лhi. The first member appears to contain the well-attested adj. haryat├б- тАШgladdeningтАЩ, but this presents certain problems: the present h├бryati does not appear with the preverb v├н and it is difficult to construct an appropriate meaning, esp. one that would harmonize with kr├бtu- тАШresolveтАЩ. Possibly, with double negation via a + v├н, тАЬwhose resolve is not undelightfulтАЭ - not a particularly compelling possibility.

Nonetheless, this derivation seems the path of least resistance and is probably responsible for GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdessen Rat nicht verschm├дht wirdтАЭ and Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬтАж nicht unbeliebt istтАЭ (possibly also HoffmannтАЩs тАЬтАж nicht zu untersch├дtzen istтАЭ - itтАЩs hard to tell). But all of these must take the -haryata- in a passive sense, although the simplex adjective never has that value.

I think itтАЩs likely that the compound involves some complex word play, scrambling and recombining the (d)h├бr─л and v├н(vrat─Б) of p─Бda a. Despite the ad hoc explanations required, IтАЩm inclined to consider the -viharyata- somehow a derivative of v├н тИЪhvс╣Ы тАШdeflect, swerve, overturnтАЩ, a well-established idiom. (RenouтАЩs тАЬdont le pouvoir est incontrariableтАЭ seems to reflect this.) Two negated nominal derivatives of this lexeme are found in the RV: ├бvihruta- тАШunswervingтАЩ, jpb: тАШnot overturnedтАЩ (V.66.2, X.170.1) and ├бvihvarant- jpb: тАШnot overturningтАЩ (IV.36.2). Unfortunately the morphological details are not going to be easy. Accounting for the loss of the v in a putative *avihvaryata- is not so difficult: it can be ascribed to dissimilation, in combination with the word play on (d)h├бr─л just mentioned. But what about the rest of the word. For the suffix -ata- I can only invoke the (small) class of -ata- adjectives with full-grade root syllable of the type dar┼Ыat├б- тАШ(lovely) to be seenтАЩ, yajat├б- тАШworthy of the sacrificeтАЩ, and the aforementioned haryat├б- тАШdelightfulтАЩ. As for the intermediate -y- between root syllable and ending, I again invoke the play on (d)h├бr─л, with the -y- representing the sandhi of -─л- before the suffix -ata-. If word play is indeed involved here, itтАЩs possible that a second reading of the first member could be тАЬnot without his fallow baysтАЭ and the whole compound means тАЬwho has no resolve without his fallow bays.тАЭ I am fully aware of what a house of cards this is and only sketch these scenarios because I think Nodhas is capable of such manipulations. I do think it possible, however, that the lack of caesura and the problematic compound are connected and that the transmitted text is not what Nodhas originally composed. It should be noted that the word division y├йn─Б viharyatakrato is also a possibility, but this doesnтАЩt help either with the lack of caesura or the analysis of the compound.

Griffith

When thy two wandering Bays thou drawest hither, thy praiser laid within thine arms the thunder,
Wherewith, O Much-invoked, in will resistless, thou smitest foemen down and many a castle.

Geldner

Wenn du, Indra, das widerspenstige Falbenpaar hertreibst, so legt der S├дnger dir die Keule in die Arme, mit der du die Feinde in die vielen Burgen treibst, du Vielgerufener, dessen Rat nicht verschm├дht wird.

Grassmann

Wenn, Indra, du die schnellen Rosse herf├╝hrst, so legt den Blitz in deinen Arm der S├дnger, Mit dem du triffst, o unaufhaltsam th├дt’ger, die Feind’ und viele Burgen, vielgerufner!

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, the best of all beings, the assailer and humiliator (of your foes), the chief ot the с╣Ъbhus, the friend of man, the subduer of enemies, did aid the young and illustrious Kutsa, and slew ┼Ъuс╣гna, in the deadly and close-fought fight.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhukс╣гa = с╣Ъbh┼лn─Бm adhipati; teс╣гu kс╣Ыtaniv─Бsaс╕е, he who abides in the с╣Ъbhus;

с╣Ъbhu = a wise man, a sage (medh─Бvin)

Jamison Brereton

You are trusty, Indra, and bold against them. You are master of the R╠еbhus, favorable to men; you are victorious.
You smashed ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa in his (war-)band, when strengthening nourishment and the axle-pin (were at stake), for the young, heaven-bright Kutsa, in partnership.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I interpret dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├║с╕е as governing the acc. et─Б╠Бn, though as a goal not a direct object..

Faithful art thou, these thou defiest, Indra; thou art the Rbhus’ Lord, heroic, victor.
Thou, by his side, for young and glorious Kutsa, with steed and car in battle slewest Susna,

Du, Indra, bist wahrhaftig, Feind bezwingend, du Ribhuherr, und mannhaft du und siegreich, Du schlugst im Felsthal auf beladnem Wagen den ├Зuschna f├╝r den sch├╢nen J├╝ngling Kutsa.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou verily did animate him to (acquire) such (renown) as that which, sender of rain and wielder of the thunderbolt, you (dis-acquire) when you slew Vс╣Ыtra, and when, munificent hero, who easily conquer (your foes) you did put to fight the Dasyus in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dasyus are enemies of Kutsa: kutsasyopakс╣гayat─Бraс╕е

Jamison Brereton

You then, Indra, as partner provided the spur, when you knotted up Vr╠еtra, you mace-bearer of bullish deeds,
when, you champion of bullish mind, you cut apart the Dasyus in their womb far away, as one who is victorious at will. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

tv├бс╣Г ha ty├бd provides the opening of the next four verses. Although ty├бd is a neut. pronoun and in 4a could function as the object of the otherwise object-less cod─лс╕е, in the following verses it does not have pronominal function; the expression X ha ty├бd is a way of providing emphasis, particular of the 2nd ps. pronoun (cf., e.g., VII.19.2, VIII.96.16-18). I would now be inclined to tr. the vss. in this sequence with тАЬIt was just you who тАжтАЭ rather than the rather recessive тАЬYou then, тАжтАЭ

Griffith

That, as a friend, thou furtheredst, O Indra, when, Thunderer, strong in act, thou crushedst Vrtra;
When, Hero, thou, great-souled, with easy conquest didst rend the Dasyus in their
distant dwelling.

Geldner

Du, Indra, hast da als Verb├╝ndeter Mut gemacht, als du tatengewaltiger Keulentr├дger den Vritra b├дndigtest, als du bullenmutiger Held in der Ferne die Dasyu┬┤s in ihrem Neste zerhiebst, m├╝helos siegend.

Grassmann

Das auch betriebst als Freund du eifrig, Indra, dass Vritra du bezwangst mit Blitz, gewalt’ger, Dass ferne du in ihrem Sitz die B├╢sen, stiermuth’ger Held, mit schnellem Sieg zerst├╝cktest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, who are unwilling to harm any resolute (mortal), set open all the quarters (of the horizon) to the horses of us who praise you, (when we are exposed) to the aversion (of our enemies); and, wielder of the thunderbolt, demolish our foes, as with a club.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You then, Indra, intending no harm to mortals, in your displeasure (you opened up the doors) even of the stronghold,
opened the barriers for the steed (that comes) from us. As if with a
deadly weapon, mace-bearer, pierce the foes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse contains many small problems of interpretation that hinder putting together the whole. IтАЩll start with the details and turn to the construction of the whole thereafter.

├бriс╣гaс╣Зyan is universally taken as intrans., patient-oriented тАШnot receiving harm, not being harmedтАЩ, but in all cases this stem is better taken as тАШnot allowing harmтАЩ.

The finite verb riс╣гaс╣Зy├бti also has this meaning тАЬintends harm, allows harmтАЩ. The parallel stem ├бriс╣гaс╣Зya- in II.29.4 has the same meaning and takes a genitive (├бriс╣гaс╣Зy─Б tan┼л╠Бn─Бm тАЬnot allowing harm to our bodiesтАЭ), and I construe the gen. m├бrt─Бn─Бm in b with ├бriс╣гyan: тАЬnot intending harm to mortals.тАЭ The next problem is dс╣Ыс╕╖h├бsya. Geldner takes this as the causer of the harm to Indra (gen. agent), while Hoffmann, followed by Witzel Got┼Н, construe it with ├бjuс╣гс╣нau, with the gen. pl. m├бrt─Бn─Бm dependent on dс╣Ыс╕╖h├бsya (Hoffmann тАЬbei Missfallen selbst eines Feststehenden unter den SterblichenтАЭ), but both the Geldner and the Witzel Got┼Н interpretations require that dс╣Ыс╕╖h├б- be a person. This is unprecedented: this past participle is virtually always used of a place, a fortified stronghold. Indra is once (VIII.44.12) called dс╣Ыс╕╖h├б-, presumably because he is as steadfast as a fortress (in the vein of тАЬa mighty fortress is our godтАЭ), but I know of no examples with people so called. If at all possible it should have the standard meaning here. I think this is possible, by reading the verb v├н тАж var of p─Бda c also with the first hemistich and supplying the word d├║raс╕е тАШdoorsтАЩ.

In fact, the other two passages containing the gen. sg. dс╣Ыс╕╖h├бsya strongly support this solution, as they both contain the verb v├н тИЪvс╣Ы and the headnoun d├║raс╕е: VI.62.11 drс╕╖╠еh├бsya cid g├│mato v├н vraj├бsya, d├║ro vartam … тАЬOpen the doors of the cattle pen, even though it is shut fastтАЭ and VII.79.4 v├н dr╠ес╕╖h├бsya d├║ro ├бdrer aurс╣Зoс╕е тАЬyou opened up the doors of the firm-fixed stone.тАЭ Note that v├н тАж var is rather more appropriate to this hemistich than it is to the p─Бda in which itтАЩs found. (Recall the double use of v├н тИЪvar in I.62.5 and 7.) The last word to be accounted for in this hemistich is ├бjuс╣гс╣нau. Unlike most tr.

I take it to be IndraтАЩs displeasure. The object of his displeasure is not expressed, but it is easy to supply тАФ presumably Vala, since Indra is opening up his stronghold. His displeasure at Vala (or other demonic enemies) is implicitly contrasted with his benevolent care not to injure mortals.

I am less sure about what p─Бda c is conveying. I assume this is a racing image: Indra starts the race by opening the barriers at the starting line. Geldner and Renou take the injunctive v├н тАж var as a functional imperative, but this is certainly not necessary. I tr.

as a past tense, in keeping with its rendering in the first hemistich, but it would be possible to take it as a present in c, as Hoffman/Witzel Got┼Н do. The phrase asm├бd ─Б╠Б тАЬ(coming) from usтАЭ seems a bit heavy simply to express that itтАЩs our horse, so there may be some racing terminology embedded here.

In d ghan├йva contains the old instr. ghan─Б╠Б. The same phrase is found in I.36.16 and IX.97.16.

Jamison Brereton Notes

tv├бс╣Г ha ty├бd provides the opening of the next four verses. Although ty├бd is a neut. pronoun and in 4a could function as the object of the otherwise object-less cod─лс╕е, in the following verses it does not have pronominal function; the expression X ha ty├бd is a way of providing emphasis, particular of the 2nd ps. pronoun (cf., e.g., VII.19.2, VIII.96.16-18). I would now be inclined to tr. the vss. in this sequence with тАЬIt was just you who тАжтАЭ rather than the rather recessive тАЬYou then, тАжтАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen invoke you, such as you are, in the thick-throned and wealth-bestowing conflict. May this your succour, powerful Indra, ever be granted in war, worthy to be enjoyed (by warriors) in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

On you then, Indra, the superior men call, at the winning of the flood, in the contest whose prize is the sun.
This help of yours here in the clash when prizes (are at stake), o
autonomous one, has become something unshakeable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The gerundive atas─Б╠Бyya- is taken by Geldner as belonging to тИЪat тАШwanderтАЩ and tr.

тАЬsoll тАж erreichbar sein,тАЭ while most (Grassmann, Renou (?), AiG II.2.286, Hoffman, Witzel Got┼Н) take it to mean тАЬto be asked for/beggedтАЭ and derived from the hapax atas─л╠Б- supposedly тАШbeggarтАЩ (VIII.3.13). But this is entirely circular, with the meaning of each of these two words determined on the basis of the other, with an occasional nod towards тИЪat тАШwanderтАЩ as their possible root (whose relevance Mayrhofer casts doubts on; see EWA s.v. atas─л╠Б-). I instead take it as a negated gerundive to тИЪtaс╣Гs тАШtug, yank, shakeтАЩ, which forms a similar gerundive to its intensive, vitantas─Б╠Бyya-. Negated gerundives do not ordinarily take accent on the privative (AiG II.1.217), and the derivational opacity of atas─Б╠Бyya- would make it likely to receive the usual -─Б╠Бyya- gerundive accent. Geldner also suggests the possibility of derivation from тИЪtaс╣Гs in a note.

Jamison Brereton Notes

tv├бс╣Г ha ty├бd provides the opening of the next four verses. Although ty├бd is a neut. pronoun and in 4a could function as the object of the otherwise object-less cod─лс╕е, in the following verses it does not have pronominal function; the expression X ha ty├бd is a way of providing emphasis, particular of the 2nd ps. pronoun (cf., e.g., VII.19.2, VIII.96.16-18). I would now be inclined to tr. the vss. in this sequence with тАЬIt was just you who тАжтАЭ rather than the rather recessive тАЬYou then, тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Hence men invoke thee, Indra, in the tumult of battle, in the light-bestowing conflict.
This aid of thine, O Godlike One, was ever to be implored in deeds of might in combat.

Geldner

Dich, Indra, rufen da die M├дnner im Kampfe, wenn es gilt, Wasser zu gewinnen, das Sonnenlicht zu erk├дmpfen. Diese deine Hilfe soll im Wettstreit, in den K├дmpfen um den Siegerpreis erreichbar sein, du Eigenartiger.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН) рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдВ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рд╣) рдЦрд▓реБ (рддреНрдпрддреН) рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХ (рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдпреЛрджреНрдзреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╛рддрд┐рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдореАрдвреЗ) рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрдп рдореАрдврдГ рд╕реЗрдЪрдирдВ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНред (рдирд░рдГ) рдирдпрдирдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдЖрдЬрд╛) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рд╣рд╡рдиреНрддреЗ) рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрджреНрдзрдиреНрддреЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрдкреНрд╕рдиреНрддреЗ (рддрд╡) (рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛рдиреНрдирдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдп рддрддреНрд╕рдореНрдмреБрджреНрдзреМ (рдЗрдпрдореН) рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛ (рдЖ) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ (рд╕рдорд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдКрддрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛ (рд╡рд╛рдЬреЗрд╖реБ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрдирд╕реЗрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ (рдЕрддрд╕рд╛рдпреНрдпрд╛) рдЕрддрдиреНрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╛ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рддрдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓рдХрд╛рджреМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХ рдЖрдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпреЛрд╜рд╕реБрдЧрд╛рдЧрдорд╢реНрдЪред рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрдгреЗрджрдВ рдкрджрдорддрдзрд╛рддреЛрд░рд╛рдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рдбрд╛рдЧрдореЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдВ рддрджрд╢реБрджреНрдзрдореН (рднреВрддреН) рднрд╡рддреБ рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, wielder of the thunderbolt, warring on behalf of Purukutsa, you did overturn the seven cities; you did cut off for Sud─Бsa wealth of Aс╣Еhas, as if (it had been a tuft) of sacred grass, and did give it to him, O king, ever satiating you (with oblations).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purukuts ais a с╣Ыс╣гi. Sud─Бsa is a king. Aс╣Еas is an asura

Jamison Brereton

You then, mace-bearing Indra, attacking, split seven fortifications for Purukutsa, one after the other.
When at will you twisted them like ritual grass for Sud─Бs, o king, from narrowness you made wide space for P┼лru.

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬone after the otherтАЭ is my attempt to render an тАЬobject-distributiveтАЭ value for the intensive dardaс╕е. (For this notion see Schaefer 1994: 86-87, though she considers dardar- lexicalized and does not attribute this sense to it, pp. 135-36.) The use of v├бrg тАШyou twistedтАЩ differs in tone in simile and frame. In the frame it is distinctly hostile and destructive, but in the simile it simply expresses the ritual action of twisting the barhis grass into seats for the visiting gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

tv├бс╣Г ha ty├бd provides the opening of the next four verses. Although ty├бd is a neut. pronoun and in 4a could function as the object of the otherwise object-less cod─лс╕е, in the following verses it does not have pronominal function; the expression X ha ty├бd is a way of providing emphasis, particular of the 2nd ps. pronoun (cf., e.g., VII.19.2, VIII.96.16-18). I would now be inclined to tr. the vss. in this sequence with тАЬIt was just you who тАжтАЭ rather than the rather recessive тАЬYou then, тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Warring for Purukutsa thou, O Indra, Thunder-armed! breakest down the seven castles;
Easily, for Sudas, like grass didst rend them, and out of need, King, broughtest gain to Puru.

Du Keulentr├дger Indra brachst da k├дmpfend die sieben Burgen f├╝r Purukutsa. Da du f├╝r Sudas die Feinde m├╝helos hinlegtest wie Opfergras, da schafftest du, o K├╢nig, dem Puru Befreiung aus Not.

Grassmann

Du, Indra, hast zerst├╢rt die sieben Burgen, o Blitzesherr, f├╝r Purukutsa k├дmpfend; Als du dem Sudas gleich wie Streu sie umwarfst, dem Puru du, o K├╢nig, aus der Noth halfst.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIncrease, divine Indra, for us throughout the earth, abundant food, (that it may be as plural ntiful) as water, by which, hero, you bestow upon us (existence), as you cause water to flow on every side.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, god Indra, will make this bright refreshment swell for us as waters do in their circling,
the refreshment with which, o champion, you will extend yourself
toward us like nourishment to flow everywhere.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─Б╠Бpaс╕е in b can certainly be the old nominative plural used as an accusative, as occasionally happens in late RV (so Grassmann and implicitly most tr.), but as I suggested elsewhere (1982: 260), it may be the nominative plural it appears to be; this may be an example of case disharmony in a simile, exploiting the ambiguities in syntax of the verb тИЪpi тАШswellтАЩ that the poets were always happy to capitalize on. In the frame p─лpayaс╕е is transitive (тАЬyou swell the refreshmentтАЭ), but in the simile intransitive (тАЬas waters [swell]тАЭ).

I take tm├бnam as functioning as a reflexive pronoun (тАЬextend yourselfтАЭ), while most tr. take it as a noun (Geldner тАШLebensgeistтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н тАШLebenshauchтАЩ). This is the only acc. to the truncated stem tm├бn-, and so its usage is hard to determine. The oblique cases (dominated by inst. tm├бn─Б) generally refer to the self (тАШby yourself, for ourselvesтАЩ, etc.), without a full-blown nominal sense, which accounts for my tr.

However, the active form of y├бс╣Гsi gives my pause, and so the standard tr. should be considered (though I am not ready to adopt it). тАЬExtend nourishment to usтАЭ seems to be formulaic, with an active form of тИЪyam, and so that voice may have prevailed here, despite the reflexive tm├бnam; cf. III.1.22 pr├б yaс╣Гsi тАж ├нс╣гo nah, IV.32.7 s├б no yandhi тАж ├нс╣гam.

Griffith

O Indra, God who movest round about us, feed us with varied food plenteous as water-
Food wherewithal, O Hero, thou bestowest vigour itself to flow to us for ever.

Geldner

Du m├╢gest uns jenes wunderbare Labsal wie die Gew├дsser in ihrem Laufe anschwellen lassen, Gott Indra, mit dem du Held uns den Lebensgeist aufrichten m├╢gest, da├Я er wie die Lebenskraft allezeit uns durchstr├╢me.

Grassmann

Du, Indra, f├╝ll uns diese reiche Labung wie Wasserfluten zu uns rings umwandelnd, Durch die du Held uns Lebenshauch verleihest, der ├╝berall wie Labetrunk uns str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraises have been offered to you, Indra, by the sons of Gotama; (they have been) uttered with reverence (to you), borne (hither) by your steeds; grant us various sorts of food. May he who has acquired wealthy by pious acts, come hither quickly in the morning.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(This hymn) has been made for you, Indra, by the Gotamas; sacred formulations have been spoken with reverence to your two fallow bay horses.
Bring a well-ornamented prize here to us. тАУ Early in the morningтАФ
soonтАФhe should come, bringing goods through his insight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply тАШhymnтАЩ as subject for ├бk─Бri in the first p─Бda and take br├бhm─Бс╣Зy ├╣kt─Б in b as a separate nominal clause. It is of course grammatically possible to take the latter phrase as subject of ├бk─Бri, since neuter plurals famously can take singular verbs.

But, fame aside, this construction is quite rare in the RV, and in this case there are two different recipients, Indra in a and the horses in b. However, I do not consider the other interpretation impossible.

Griffith

Prayers have been made by Gotamas, O Indra, addressed to thee, with laud for thy Bay Horses.
Bring us in noble shape abundant riches. May he, enriched with prayer, come soon and early.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рд░реВрдк рд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрджрд┐ рднреА рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдзрди рдФрд░ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее реп рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░, рд╕рднрд╛рджреНрдпрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдФрд░ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рд╕рдордЭрдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рд╕рднрд╛рджреНрдпрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ ! рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдпреИрд░реНрдЧреЛрддрдореЗрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреИрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реИрд░реНрдирдорд╕рд╛ рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рдиреНрдпреЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпрдХрд╛рд░рд┐ рддреИрдГ рд╕рд╣ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реБрдГ рд╕реБрдкреЗрд╢рд╕рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░реНрдЬрдЧрдореНрдпрд╛рджреЗрддрджреНрднрд░реЗрдЪреНрдЪ рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдореЗрдирддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдордХреНрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рднрд░ рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕рднрд╛рджреНрдпрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ (рдЧреЛрддрдореЗрднрд┐рдГ) рдпреЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реБрднрд╛рдиреН рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдВрд╕реНрддреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ред рдЧреМрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рдкрджрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрек.рез) (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐) рдмреГрд╣рддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ (рдУрдХреНрддрд╛) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдирдорд╕рд╛) рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрдиред рдирдо рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.рен) рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.реи) (рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд╣рд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдмрд▓рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН (рд╕реБрдкреЗрд╢рд╕рдореН) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреЗрд╢рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддрдореН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдХрд░рдореН (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рднрд░) рдзрд░ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдореН (рдордХреНрд╖реБ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдореН (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реБрдГ) рдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдЦреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддрд╛ (рдЬрдЧрдореНрдпрд╛рддреН) рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
